	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Eid al-Fitr</i></h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_ul-Fitr&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a>)</span></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Islamic holiday that marks the end of Ramadan</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Hari Raya" redirects here. For Feast of the Sacrifice which is also known as Hari Raya in several countries, see <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="hd" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: lightgreen"><i>Eid al-Fitr</i></th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Official name</th><td><a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">عيد الفطر</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">‘Īd al-Fiṭr</i></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Observed&#160;by</th><td><a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Type</th><td><a href="/wiki/Muslim_holidays" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim holidays">Islamic</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Significance</th><td class="summary">Marks the end of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_(calendar_month)" title="Ramadan (calendar month)">Ramadan</a> <a href="/wiki/Sawm" class="mw-redirect" title="Sawm">fasting</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Celebrations</th><td><a href="/wiki/Eid_prayers" title="Eid prayers">Eid prayers</a>, charity, social gatherings, festive meals, <a href="/wiki/Eidi_(gift)" title="Eidi (gift)">gift-giving</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Observances</th><td><a href="/wiki/Eid_prayers" title="Eid prayers">Eid prayers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zak%C4%81t" class="mw-redirect" title="Zakāt">charity-giving</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date</th><td>1 <a href="/wiki/Shawwal" title="Shawwal">Shawwal</a><sup id="cite_ref-ummalqura_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ummalqura-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">2019&#160;date</th><td>4 June<sup id="cite_ref-ummalqura_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ummalqura-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> (Saudi Arabia and some other countries)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
5 June (Pakistan and some other countries)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">2020&#160;date</th><td>24 May (expected<sup id="cite_ref-ummalqura_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ummalqura-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>&#160;– may differ 1 day dependent on sighting of lunar crescent)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Related&#160;to</th><td><a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i><b>Eid al-Fitr</b></i> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span></span> <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/əl/: &#39;le&#39; in &#39;bottle&#39;">əl</span></span> <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">eed əl <span style="font-size:90%">FIT</span>-ər</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">عيد الفطر</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="American Library Association – Library of Congress transliteration">ʻĪd al-Fiṭr</i></i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Arabic" title="Help:IPA/Arabic">[ʕiːd al fitˤr]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> also called the "<b>Festival of Breaking the Fast</b>", is a <a href="/wiki/Religious_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious holiday">religious holiday</a> celebrated by <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> worldwide that marks the end of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> holy month of <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fasting</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Fasting_in_Islam" title="Fasting in Islam">ṣawm</a></i>). This religious Eid (<a href="/wiki/Muslim_holidays" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim holidays">Muslim religious festival</a>) is the first and only day in the month of <a href="/wiki/Shawwal" title="Shawwal">Shawwal</a> during which Muslims are not permitted to fast. The holiday celebrates the conclusion of the 29 or 30 days of dawn-to-sunset fasting during the entire <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_(calendar_month)" title="Ramadan (calendar month)">month of Ramadan</a>. The day of Eid, therefore, falls on the first day of the month of Shawwal. The date for the start of any <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calendar" title="Islamic calendar">lunar Hijri</a> month varies based on when the new moon is sighted by local religious authorities, so the exact day of celebration varies by locality.
</p><p>Eid al-Fitr has a particular <a href="/wiki/Salat" class="mw-redirect" title="Salat">salat</a> (Islamic prayer) consisting of two <a href="/wiki/Rakat" title="Rakat">rakats</a> (units) and generally offered in an open field or large hall. It may be performed only in congregation (<i>jamāʿat</i>) and has an additional extra six <a href="/wiki/Takbir" title="Takbir">Takbirs</a> (raising of the hands to the ears while saying "Allāhu ʾAkbar" which means "God is the greatest"), three of them in the beginning of the first raka'ah and three of them just before <a href="/wiki/Ruku" title="Ruku">rukūʿ</a> in the second raka'ah in the <a href="/wiki/Hanafi" title="Hanafi">Hanafi</a> school of <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Other Sunni schools usually have twelve Takbirs, seven in the first, and five at the beginning of the second raka'ah. According to <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a>, it has 6 Takbirs in the first Rakat at the end of qira'a, before rukūʿ, and 5 in the second.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> This Eid al-Fitr salat is, depending on which juristic opinion is followed, <i><a href="/wiki/Fard" title="Fard">farḍ</a></i> <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">فرض</span> (obligatory), <i><a href="/wiki/Mustahabb" title="Mustahabb">mustaḥabb</a></i> <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">مستحب</span> (strongly recommended, just short of obligatory) or <i>mandūb</i> <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">مندوب</span> (preferable).
</p><p>Muslims believe that they are commanded by God, as mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>, to continue their fast until the last day of Ramadan<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and pay the <a href="/wiki/Zakat_al-Fitr" title="Zakat al-Fitr">Zakat al-Fitr</a> before offering the <a href="/wiki/Eid_prayers" title="Eid prayers">Eid prayers</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eid al-Fitr was originated by the <a href="/wiki/Prophets_of_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Prophets of Islam"> Islamic prophet</a> <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>. It is observed on the first day of the Islamic month of <a href="/wiki/Shawwal" title="Shawwal">Shawwal</a> at the end of the month of Ramadan, during which Muslims undergo a period of fasting.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to certain <a href="/wiki/Ahadith" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahadith">traditions</a>, these festivals were initiated in Medina after the <a href="/wiki/Hijra_(Islam)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hijra (Islam)">migration of Muhammad from Mecca</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anas_bin_Malik" class="mw-redirect" title="Anas bin Malik">Anas</a> (R.A) reports: When the Prophet arrived in Madinah, he found people celebrating two specific days in which they used to entertain themselves with recreation and merriment. He asked them about the nature of these festivities at which they replied that these days were occasions of fun and recreation. At this, the Prophet remarked that the Almighty has fixed two days [of festivity] instead of these for you which are better than these: Eid al-Fitr and <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_rituals">General rituals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: General rituals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Eid_cuisine" title="Eid cuisine">Eid cuisine</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calendar#Astronomical_considerations" title="Islamic calendar">Islamic calendar §&#160;Astronomical considerations</a></div>
<p>Traditionally, it is the day (beginning at sunset) of the first sighting of the <a href="/wiki/Hilal_(crescent_moon)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hilal (crescent moon)">crescent moon</a> shortly after sunset. If the moon is not observed immediately after the 29th day of the previous lunar month (either because clouds block its view or because the western sky is still too bright when the moon sets), then it is the following day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Eid al-Fitr is celebrated for one, two or three days. It is <a href="/wiki/Haraam" class="mw-redirect" title="Haraam">forbidden</a> to fast on the Day of Eid. Also, a specific <a href="/wiki/Prayer" title="Prayer">prayer</a> is nominated for this day.<sup id="cite_ref-Deborah_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deborah-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As an obligatory act of charity, money is paid to the poor and the needy (Arabic: <i>Zakat-ul-fitr</i>) before performing the ‘Eid prayer.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> . As another rituals, Muslims praise God in a loud voice while going to the Eid prayer: <i>Allāhu Akbar, Allāhu Akbar, Allāhu Akbar. Lā ilāha illà l-Lāh wal-Lāhu akbar, Allahu akbar walil-Lāhi l-ḥamd</i>. Recitation ceases when they get to the place of Eid or once the Imam commences activities.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG/220px-Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG/330px-Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG/440px-Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1701" data-file-height="1276" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Istiqlal_Mosque_Eid_ul_Fitr_Jamaah_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eid al-Fitr mass prayer in <a href="/wiki/Istiqlal_Mosque,_Jakarta" title="Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta">Istiqlal Mosque, Jakarta</a>, Indonesia</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eid_prayer_and_eidgah">Eid prayer and <i>eidgah</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Eid prayer and eidgah">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eidgah" title="Eidgah">Eidgah</a></div>
<p>The Eid prayer is performed in congregation in open areas like fields, community centres, etc. or at mosques. No <a href="/wiki/Adhan" title="Adhan">call to prayer</a> is given for this Eid prayer, and it consists of only two <a href="/wiki/Raka%CA%BF%C4%81t" class="mw-redirect" title="Rakaʿāt">units of prayer</a> with an additional six <a href="/wiki/Takbir" title="Takbir">Takbirs</a>. The Eid prayer is followed by the <a href="/wiki/Khutbah" title="Khutbah">sermon</a> and then a <a href="/wiki/Dua" title="Dua">supplication</a> asking for Allah's forgiveness, mercy, peace and blessings for all living beings across the world. The sermon also instructs Muslims as to the performance of rituals of Eid, such as the <a href="/wiki/Zak%C4%81t" class="mw-redirect" title="Zakāt">zakat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Listening to the sermon at Eid is not required and is optional, a <a href="/wiki/Sunnah" title="Sunnah">Sunnah</a> i.e. while the sermon is being delivered. After the prayers, Muslims visit their relatives, friends and acquaintances or hold large communal celebrations in homes, community centres or rented halls.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Eid gifts, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Eidi_(gift)" title="Eidi (gift)">Eidi</a></i>, are frequently given at eid to children and immediate relatives.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_Eid-ul-fitr_prayer">Performing Eid-ul-fitr prayer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Performing Eid-ul-fitr prayer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eid al-Fitr prayer (Salat al-Eid) or Eid al-Fitr Namaz is performed on the occasion of Eid. The Prayer of Eid al-Fitr is performed in two different ways by Sunni and <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> Islam.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sunni_Procedure">Sunni Procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sunni Procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are two Rak'ah (Rakaat) performed in the Eid al-Fitr prayer.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The prayer of Eid al-Fitr starts by doing "Niyyat" for the prayer and then Takbeer (Allahu Akbar) is said by the <a href="/wiki/Imam" title="Imam">Imam</a> and all the followers. The next is to recite "Takbeer-e-Tehreema" in first Rakaat. Then the congregation says Allahu Akbar three times, every time raising hands to the ears and dropping them except the last time when hands are folded. Then the Imam reads the Surah-e-Fatiha and other Surah. Then the congregation performs Ruku and <a href="/wiki/Sujud" title="Sujud">Sujud</a> as in other prayers. This completes the first Rak’ah. Then the congregation rises up from the first Rak'ah and folds hands for the second Rak’ah. In the next step the Imam recites Surah Fatiha and another Surah and after this 3 Takbirs are called out just before the Ruku; each time raising hands to the ears and dropping them.Then for the fourth time the congregation says Allah o Akbar and goes into the Ruku. The rest of the prayer is completed in the regular manner. This completes the Eid prayer. After the prayer there is a <a href="/wiki/Khutbah" title="Khutbah">khutbah</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1984_%22Fetr_Feast%22_stamp_of_Iran.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/1984_%22Fetr_Feast%22_stamp_of_Iran.jpg/220px-1984_%22Fetr_Feast%22_stamp_of_Iran.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/1984_%22Fetr_Feast%22_stamp_of_Iran.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="261" data-file-height="374" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1984_%22Fetr_Feast%22_stamp_of_Iran.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eid Fetr, in Iran (1984)</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shia_procedure">Shia procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Shia procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Shia also perform two Rak’ah in the Eid al-Fitr prayer. Prayer starts with the Niyyat followed by the five "Takbeers". During every "Takbeer" of the first Rak’ah, a special Dua is recited. Then the Imam recites Sūrat al-Fātiḥah and Surat Al-'A`lá and the congregation performs Ruku and Sujud as in other prayers. In the second Rak’ah again the same above steps (five Takbeers, Sūrat al-Fātiḥah and Surat Al-'A`lá, Ruku and Sujud) are repeated. After the prayer, Khutbah starts.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_tradition">Islamic tradition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Islamic tradition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azeri_carpet_(Sirvan_group).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Azeri_carpet_%28Sirvan_group%29.jpg/220px-Azeri_carpet_%28Sirvan_group%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Azeri_carpet_%28Sirvan_group%29.jpg/330px-Azeri_carpet_%28Sirvan_group%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Azeri_carpet_%28Sirvan_group%29.jpg/440px-Azeri_carpet_%28Sirvan_group%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1081" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azeri_carpet_(Sirvan_group).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Many <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> often bring prayer rugs to the Mosque on Eid al-Fitr.</div></div></div>
<p>Eid al-Fitr marks the end of the fasting month of Ramadan. This has to do with the communal aspects of the fast, which expresses many of the basic values of the <a href="/wiki/Ummah" title="Ummah">Muslim community</a>; e.g., empathy for the poor, charity, worship, steadfastness, patience etc. Fasting is also believed by some scholars to extol fundamental distinctions, lauding the power of the <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> realm, while acknowledging the subordination of the physical realm. It also teaches a Muslim to stay away from worldly desires and to focus entirely on the Lord and thank Him for his blessings. It is a rejuvenation of the religion and it creates a stronger bond between the Muslim and his Lord.<sup id="cite_ref-Ritual_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ritual-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Practices_by_country">Practices by country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Practices by country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Saudi Arabia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Eid al-Fitr is celebrated with great pomp in Saudi Arabia. Saudis decorate their homes and prepare sumptuous meals for family and friends.
Eid festivities in Saudi Arabia may vary culturally depending on the region, but one common thread in all celebrations is of generosity and hospitality. First, it is common Saudi tradition for families to gather at the patriarchal home after the Eid prayers. Before the special Eid meal is served, young children will line up in front of each adult family member, who dispense money as gifts to the children. Family members will also typically have a time where they will pass out gift bags to the children. These bags are often beautifully decorated and contain candies and toys.Many shopkeepers will show their generosity at Eid providing free Eid gifts with each purchase. For example, during Eid, many of the chocolate shops will give each customer who buys a selection of candies a free crystal candy dish with their purchase.
In the spirit of Eid, many Saudis go out of their way to show their kindness and generosity. It is common for even complete strangers to greet one another at random, even by occupants of vehicles waiting at stop lights. Sometimes even toys and gifts will be given to children by complete strangers. It is traditional for Saudi men to go and buy large quantities of rice and other staples, and then leave them anonymously at the doors of those who are less fortunate. During Eid morning and after the Eid prayer, people in some areas of the middle of Saudi Arabia (such as Al Qassim) host large communal meals. Celebrants put large rugs on one of the streets of their neighborhood, and households prepare a large meal to be shared by all neighbors. It is common practice for people to swap places to try more than one kind of meal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the major cities of Saudi Arabia, every night there are huge fireworks shows.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Iran">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_al-Fitr_prayer,_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Eid_al-Fitr_prayer%2C_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg/220px-Eid_al-Fitr_prayer%2C_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Eid_al-Fitr_prayer%2C_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg/330px-Eid_al-Fitr_prayer%2C_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Eid_al-Fitr_prayer%2C_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg/440px-Eid_al-Fitr_prayer%2C_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_al-Fitr_prayer,_Bandar_Torkaman_-_26_June_2017_08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view from wherever <a href="/wiki/Eid_prayers" title="Eid prayers">Eid al-Fitr prayer</a> held outside the Iranian city of <a href="/wiki/Bandar_Torkaman" title="Bandar Torkaman">Bandar Torkaman</a> on June 26, 2017.</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, at the last days of the month of Ramadan, several groups of experts representating the office of <a href="/wiki/Ali_Khamenei" title="Ali Khamenei">Ayatollah Khamenei</a> go to the different zones of the country. They determine that Eid al-Fitr is to begin by the new moon's crescent, as sign of the starting of each lunar month in the Islamic calendar is seen and confirmed by these groups.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Iranian Muslims celebrate the first day of the month of Shawwal as the Eid al-Fitr, signifying that the fasting month has ended. They take part in the Eid al-Fitr special prayer that generally takes place in an open field or a large hall with a congregation in attendance, and pay the Zakat al-Fitr.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
The Eid al-Fitr prayer has been led by Ayatollah Seyyed Ali Khamenei, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran" title="Supreme Leader of Iran">Supreme Leader of Iran</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ruhollah_Khomeini" title="Ruhollah Khomeini">Imam Khomeini</a> Grand Prayer Grounds (Mossalla) and he delivers the sermon after the prayer.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
Also in Iran, there are usually one or two days as a national holiday marking the celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg/220px-Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg/330px-Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg/440px-Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_mahya3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Bayram_(Turkey)" title="Bayram (Turkey)">Bayram</a> wishes from the Istanbul Metropolitan Municipality, stating "Let us love, Let us be loved", in the form of mahya lights stretched across the <a href="/wiki/Minaret" title="Minaret">minarets</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Ahmed_Mosque_(Istanbul)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultan Ahmed Mosque (Istanbul)">Blue Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, nationwide celebrated holidays are referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Bayram_(Turkey)" title="Bayram (Turkey)">bayram</a></i>, and Eid al-Fitr is referred to as both <i>Şeker Bayramı</i> ("Bayram of Sweets") and <i>Ramazan Bayramı</i> ("Ramadan Bayram"). It is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Turkey" title="Public holidays in Turkey">public holiday</a>, where schools and government offices are generally closed for the entire three-day period of the celebrations. The celebrations of this <i>bayram</i> are infused with national traditions. It is customary for people to greet one another with <i>Bayramınız kutlu olsun</i> ("May your <i>bayram</i> be blessed"<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>) or <i>Bayramınız mübarek olsun</i> ("May your <i>bayram</i> be blessed"). <i>Mutlu Bayramlar</i> ("Happy <i>Bayram</i>") is an alternative phrase for celebrating this <i>bayram</i>. It is a time for people to attend prayer services, put on their best clothes (referred to as <i>bayramlık</i>, often purchased just for the occasion), visit all their loved ones (such as relatives, neighbours, and friends), and pay their respects to the deceased with organised visits to cemeteries, where large, temporary <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaars</a> of flowers, water (for watering the plants adorning a grave), and prayer books are set up for the three-day occasion. The first day of the <i>bayram</i> is generally regarded as the most important, with all members of the family waking up early, and the men going to their neighbourhood mosques for the special <i>bayram</i> prayer. It is regarded as especially important to honour elderly citizens by kissing their right hand and placing it on one's forehead while wishing them <i>bayram</i> greetings. It is also customary for young children to go around their neighbourhood, door to door, and wish everyone a "Happy <i>Bayram</i>", for which they are awarded candy, chocolates, traditional sweets such as <a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">baklava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Delight" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Delight">Turkish Delight</a>, or a small amount of money at every door, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Hallowe%27en" class="mw-redirect" title="Hallowe&#39;en">Hallowe'en</a> custom in the United States.Municipalities all around the country organise fund-raising events for the poor, in addition to public shows such as concerts or more traditional forms of entertainment such as the <a href="/wiki/Karag%C3%B6z_and_Hacivat" title="Karagöz and Hacivat">Karagöz and Hacivat</a> <a href="/wiki/Shadow_play" title="Shadow play">shadow-theatre</a> and even performances by the <i><a href="/wiki/Ottoman_military_band" title="Ottoman military band">Mehter</a></i>&#160;– a <a href="/wiki/Janissary" class="mw-redirect" title="Janissary">Janissary</a> Band founded during the days of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Eid al-Fitr</i> is a three-day feast and an official holiday in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> with vacations for schools, universities and government offices. Some stores and restaurants are also closed during Eid. The Eid day starts with a small snack followed by Eid prayers in congregation attended by men, women, and children in which the sermon reminds Egyptians of the virtues and good deeds they should do unto others, even strangers, during Eid and throughout the year. Afterwards, neighbors, friends, and relatives start greeting one another. The most common greeting is "Eid Mubarak" (Blessed Eid). Family visits are considered a must on the first day of the Eid, so they have the other two days to enjoy by going to parks, cinemas, theatres or the beaches. Some like to go on tours or a Nile cruise, but Sharm El Sheikh is also considered a favorite spot for spending holidays in Egypt.Children are normally given new clothes to wear throughout the Eid. Also, women (particularly mothers, wives, sisters and daughters) are commonly given special gifts by their loved ones. It is customary for children to also receive a <i>Eid-ey-yah</i> from their adult relatives. This is a small sum of money that the children receive and is used to spend on all their activities throughout the Eid. Children will wear their new clothes and go out to amusement parks, gardens or public courtyards based on how much their Eidyah affords. The amusement parks can range from the huge ones on the outskirts of Cairo-Nile, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Felucca_Nile&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Felucca Nile (page does not exist)">Felucca Nile</a> rides is one common feature of Eid celebration in Egyptian villages, towns and cities. The families gatherings involve cooking and eating all kinds of Egyptian food like Fata, but the items most associated with Eid al-Fitr are <a href="/wiki/Kahk" title="Kahk">Kahk</a> (singular = Kahka), which are cookies filled with nuts and covered with powdered sugar. Egyptians either bake it at home or buy it in the bakery. Thus, a bakery crowded in the last few days of Ramadan with Kahk buyers is a common scene. TV in Egypt celebrates Eid too, with a continuous marathon of movies as well as programmes featuring live interviews from all over Egypt of both public figures and everyday citizens, sharing their Eid celebrations. For a lot of families from working neighbourhoods, the Eid celebration also means small mobile neighbourhood rides, much like a neighbourhood carnival. In a lot of neighbourhood courtyards, kids also gather around a storyteller, a puppeteer or a magician mesmerised by Egyptian folktales or by a grownup's sleight of hand. It is also customary for kids to rent decorated bikes to ride around town.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Egyptians like to celebrate with others so the streets are always crowded during the days and nights of Eid.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Heightened_incidence_of_sexual_assault_during_Eid_al-Fitr">Heightened incidence of sexual assault during Eid al-Fitr</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Heightened incidence of sexual assault during Eid al-Fitr">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rape_in_Egypt" title="Rape in Egypt">Rape in Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mass_sexual_assault_in_Egypt" title="Mass sexual assault in Egypt">Mass sexual assault in Egypt</a></div>
<p>There are several accounts of a heightened number of <a href="/wiki/Rape_in_Egypt" title="Rape in Egypt">sexual assaults and rapes</a> taking place during the festival in 2006 in Egypt, some noting as well the precautions being taken to prevent a recurrence of such problems.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent reports indicate that this phenomenon continues to cause concern,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Al_Arabiya_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al_Arabiya-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> one Egyptian journalist writes, 'The Eid al-Fitr holiday following this year's Ramadan brought its usual share of sexual harassment'.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Operation_Anti_Sexual_Harassment" title="Operation Anti Sexual Harassment">Operation Anti Sexual Harassment</a>, an Egyptian organisation founded to protect against sexual assaults, described Eid al-Fitr as a "season for harassment",<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the prevalence of such attacks 'a trend that has become associated with Eid al-Fitr celebrations in recent years'.<sup id="cite_ref-Al_Arabiya_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al_Arabiya-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 allegations also surfaced in Cairo and Tanta.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Public discussion has been reported to be difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> 2014 saw lower rates of attempted harassment, and activists reported more confidence since amendment of the penal code.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> 141 police reports for harassment were filed in Cairo in 2015, though it was claimed many reports were withdrawn.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> 2016 saw a reduction to 120 complaints and 35 arrests for harassment,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> many women however felt it necessary to take precautions.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> 2018 showed some evidence of significant reduction.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Edward Lane also alludes to a problem with 'intrigues' with females around Eid al Fitr, in the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_in_Morocco.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Eid_in_Morocco.JPG/220px-Eid_in_Morocco.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Eid_in_Morocco.JPG/330px-Eid_in_Morocco.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Eid_in_Morocco.JPG/440px-Eid_in_Morocco.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_in_Morocco.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eid al-Fitr mass prayer in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a></div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since 2012, <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> sees three days of celebration, with only 2 days as a national holiday (1st Eid and second Eid), with preparations starting several days earlier. Special biscuits are made to give to friends and relatives on the day, including <a href="/wiki/Baklava" title="Baklava">Baklawa</a> and several kinds of "<a href="/wiki/Ka%27ak" title="Ka&#39;ak">ka'ak</a>". Men will go to the mosque early in the morning, while the women will either go with them or stay in and prepare for the celebration by putting together new outfits and toys for their children, as well as a big family lunch generally held at one of the parents' homes. During the daylight hours, there may be dancing and music, but the feasting lasts all day long, and many gifts are a large part of tradition. Also, food is the centre of this holiday, so this is one of the highlights of the evening. Different members of a family visit each other. Usually, children accompany their father and visit aunts, uncles, grandparents and friends to congratulate them on the Eid. They will be offered drinks and special cookies. Women will stay at home with some of the children in order to welcome members of the family that come to visit and congratulate for the end of the fasting.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Somalia">Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_(14587452130).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_%2814587452130%29.jpg/220px-EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_%2814587452130%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_%2814587452130%29.jpg/330px-EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_%2814587452130%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_%2814587452130%29.jpg/440px-EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_%2814587452130%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5235" data-file-height="3470" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EIDUL_FITRI_IN_BAIDOA_Eidul_Fitr_in_-1-9.jpg_(14587452130).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eid al-Fitr prayers in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a></div></div></div>
<p>In Somalia and other Islamic parts of the Horn region, Eid al-Fitr is observed by the Muslim communities. Celebrations marking the event are typically accompanied by elaborate banquets, where special dishes such as <i>xalwo</i> (halwo) and buskut (buskuit) are served.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg/220px-Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg/330px-Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg/440px-Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="450" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_celebration_2014_in_Durban.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Muslims in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> celebrating Eid al-Fitr</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, hundreds of Muslims will gather at <a href="/wiki/Green_Point,_Cape_Town" title="Green Point, Cape Town">Green Point</a> in the evening of the last day of Ramadan each year for the sighting of the moon. The gathering brings together people from all walks of life, and everyone comes with something to share with others at the time of breaking the fast. The <a href="/wiki/Maghrib" class="mw-redirect" title="Maghrib">Maghrib</a> (sunset) prayer is then performed in congregation and the formal moon-sighting results are announced thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The festival of Eid al-Fitr is celebrated by first attending the mosque in the morning for Eid prayer. This is followed by visiting relatives and neighbours. Children receive presents and money from elder members of the family, relatives and neighbours. Most people wear new clothes with bright colours, while biscuits, cakes, <a href="/wiki/Samosa" title="Samosa">samosas</a>, pies and <a href="/wiki/Tart" title="Tart">tarts</a> are presented to visitors as treats. Lunch is usually served in family groups. It is also customary to exchange gifts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sudan">Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, where 97% of the population is Muslim,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> preparations for Eid begin the last couple of days in Ramadan. For days, <i>ka'ak</i> (sugar powdered cookies), <i>bettifour</i> (dry baked goods including dainty biscuits, baked meringues and macaroons&#160;– whose name are derived from the French <i>petit four</i>) and popcorn are baked in large batches to serve to guests and to give to family and friends; dressy Eid clothes are either shopped for or sewn; girls and women decorate their hands and feet with <a href="/wiki/Henna" title="Henna">henna</a>; and parts of the house may even be painted. The night before Eid, the whole household partakes in cleaning the house and yard and setting out the finest bedsheets, table cloths, and decorations. On the day of Eid, men and boys (and occasionally women and girls) will attend the Eid prayer. For the next 3 days, families will then partake in visiting each other, extended family, neighbours, and close friends. In these short visits, the baked goods, chocolates and sweets are served, and often large lunches are prepared for the visiting well-wishers. Children are given gifts, either in the form of toys or money.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria">Nigeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Nigeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> is officially a secular country populated by large numbers of Muslims and Christians. Eid is popularly known as "Small Sallah" in Nigeria and people generally greet each other with the traditional greeting: "Barka Da Sallah", which means "Greetings on Sallah" in the <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">Hausa language</a>. Muslims observe their Eid prayers at designated praying grounds before heading home to partake in festive meals, generally prepared by the women of the household. The <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Nigeria" title="Public holidays in Nigeria">Federal holiday</a> typically lasts for three days in Nigeria.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia">South Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: South Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Afghanistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the predominantly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> Muslim culture of <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, Eid al-Fitr holds significant importance and is celebrated widely for three days. The most common greeting is <i>Eid Mubarak</i> (Blessed Eid). This Eid among the Pashto-speaking community is called <i>Kochnai Akhtar</i>. Afghans start preparing for the Eid al-Fitr festival up to ten days prior by cleaning up their homes. The practice is called <i>Khana Takani</i> in Dari. Afghans visit their local bazaars to buy new clothes, sweets and snacks. Special treats served to guests during the festivities during Eid are: <i>Jelabi</i> (<a href="/wiki/Jalebi" title="Jalebi">Jalebi</a>), <i>Shor-Nakhod</i> (made with chickpeas), and <i>Cake wa Kolcha</i> (a simple cake, similar to pound cake). On the day of Eid al-Fitr, Afghans will first offer their Eid prayers and then gather in their homes with their families, greeting one another by saying "<i>Eid Mubarak</i>" and usually adding "<i>Eidet Mobarak Roza wa Namazet Qabool Dakhel Hajiha wa Ghaziha,</i>" which means "Happy Eid to you; may your fasting and prayers be accepted by Allah, and may you be counted among those who will go to the Hajj-pilgrimage." Family elders will give money and gifts to children. It is also common practice to visit families and friends, which may be difficult to do at other times of the year. Children walk from home to home saying "<i>Khala Eidet Mubarak</i>" ("aunt happy Eid"), and they receive cookies or <i>Pala</i>. At night multiple campfires will be set around houses, some to the point that entire valleys may initially appear to be engulfed in flame. Celebratory fire with automatic rifles, particularly tracer rounds, can also be expected in high density.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.,_1843.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.%2C_1843.jpg/220px-A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.%2C_1843.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="69" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.%2C_1843.jpg/330px-A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.%2C_1843.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.%2C_1843.jpg/440px-A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.%2C_1843.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3915" data-file-height="1230" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_panorama_in_12_folds_showing_the_procession_of_the_Emperor_Bahadur_Shah_to_celebrate_the_feast_of_the_%27Id.,_1843.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A panorama in 12 folds showing an imperial Eid al-Fitr procession by <a href="/wiki/Bahadur_Shah_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahadur Shah II">Bahadur Shah II</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg/220px-Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg/330px-Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg/440px-Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="1026" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Babur_greets_courtiers_at_the_Id_festival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Mughal Emperor">Mughal Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Babur" title="Babur">Babur</a> greets courtiers during the Eid al-Fitr festival</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, Eid al-Fitr is also referred to as both <i>Meethi Eid میٹھی عید</i> ("Sweet Eid") and <i>Choti Eid چھوٹی عید</i> ("Small Eid"). On the day of Eid al-Fitr, people wear new clothes to get ready for Eid prayer. People are supposed to give obligatory charity on behalf of each of their family member to the needy or poor before Eid day or at least before Eid prayer. This will allow everybody to share the joy of Eid and not feel depressed. There is three days' national holiday for Eid celebration, while festivities and greetings tradition usually continues for the whole month. There is also a tradition that has developed in the recent past of people sending Eid greeting cards to distant family members, relatives and friends. For Eid prayer, people gather at large open areas like sports grounds, parks or large open area. After Eid Salat people meet and greet each other with traditional hug of friendship and the greeting "Eid Mubarak". Before going home people give charity to needy and the poor, to further make it possible to have everybody be able to enjoy the day. On their way home, people buy sweets, gas balloons for kids, and gifts for the family. At home family members enjoy special Eid breakfast with various types of sweets and desserts, including traditional dessert <a href="/wiki/Sheer_khurma" title="Sheer khurma">sheer khurma</a>, which is made of vermicelli, milk, butter, dry fruits and dates, etc. Eid is mainly enjoyed by the kids, as they mostly receive money in cash called "<a href="/wiki/Eidi_(gift)" title="Eidi (gift)">Eidi</a>" as gift by every elder in the family and relatives when they visit their places. On Eid day kids are allowed to spend their gift money (Eidi) as they want. Media also cover Eid festivities all day and air various special programmes on TV for all age groups.Games and outdoor amusements such as fairground rides are enjoyed all day. People visit their elders relatives first then others and friends all day and share the joy of the day. Some go to parks, seaside, rivers, historical monuments or lake fronts to enjoy and relax. Family get together in the evening to enjoy Eid dinner, and plan how to celebrate second and third day of Eid.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mehndi_design.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mehndi_design.jpg/120px-Mehndi_design.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mehndi_design.jpg/180px-Mehndi_design.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mehndi_design.jpg/240px-Mehndi_design.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mehndi_design.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mehndi" title="Mehndi">Mehndi</a> is the application of <a href="/wiki/Henna" title="Henna">henna</a> as a temporary form of skin decoration, commonly applied during Eid al-Fitr.</div></div></div>
<p>Celebrations in India and the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> share many similarities with regional variations, because a large part of the Indian subcontinent was ruled as one nation during the days of the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>. The night before Eid is called <a href="/wiki/Chaand_Raat" title="Chaand Raat">Chaand Raat</a>, which means, "Night of the Moon". Muslims in these countries will often visit bazaars and shopping malls with their families for Eid shopping. Women, especially younger girls, often apply the traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Mehndi" title="Mehndi">Mehndi</a></i>, or henna, on their hands and feet and wear colourful bangles. The traditional Eid greeting is <i>Eid Mubarak</i>, and it is frequently followed by a formal embrace. Gifts are frequently given—new clothes are part of the tradition—and it is also common for children to be given small sums of money (<i>Eidi</i>) by their elders. It is common for children to offer <i><a href="/wiki/S-L-M" class="mw-redirect" title="S-L-M">salam</a></i> to parents and adult relatives.After the Eid prayers, it is common for some families to visit graveyards and pray for the salvation of departed family members. It is also common to visit neighbours, family members, friends and to get together to share sweets, snacks and special meals including some special dishes that are prepared specifically on Eid.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Special celebratory dishes in India, Pakistan, and Bangladesh include <i>Lachcha</i>/<i>লাচ্চা</i> or <i>sivayyan</i>/<i>শিমাই</i>, a dish of fine, toasted sweet <a href="/wiki/Vermicelli" title="Vermicelli">vermicelli</a> noodles with milk and dried fruit (see <a href="/wiki/Sheer_khurma" title="Sheer khurma">Sheer khurma</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jama_Maszid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Jama_Maszid.jpg/500px-Jama_Maszid.jpg" decoding="async" width="500" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Jama_Maszid.jpg/750px-Jama_Maszid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Jama_Maszid.jpg/1000px-Jama_Maszid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11418" data-file-height="2930" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jama_Maszid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eid al-Fitr mass prayer at <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jama_Masjid,_Delhi" title="Jama Masjid, Delhi">Jama Masjid</a></div></div></div>
<p>On Eid day before prayers, people distribute a charity locally known as <i>fitrana</i>. Many people also avail themselves of this opportunity to distribute zakat, an Islamic obligatory <a href="/wiki/Alms" title="Alms">alms</a> tax of 2.5% of one's annual savings, to the needy. Zakat is often distributed in the form of food and new clothes. In India, there are many popular places for Muslims to congregate to perform Eid prayers at this time include the <a href="/wiki/Jama_Masjid,_Delhi" title="Jama Masjid, Delhi">Jama Masjid</a> in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mecca_Masjid" class="mw-redirect" title="Mecca Masjid">Mecca Masjid</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad</a>, Aishbagh Idgah in <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>, Red Road and Nakhoda Masjid in <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, Taj-ul Masjid in <a href="/wiki/Bhopal" title="Bhopal">Bhopal</a>, Jama Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, Hazratbal Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a>. Muslims turn out in the thousands, as there is a lot of excitement surrounding the celebration of this festival. It is common for some Hindus to visit their Muslim friends and neighbours on Eid to convey their greetings.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Eid al-Fitr is commonly known in Bangladesh as 'Romjaner Eid' and is observed over a three-day public holiday in Bangladesh. Educational institutions, banks and corporate offices usually remain closed for almost a week during this time. Bangladeshis observe the holiday by performing the obligatory Eid prayers on the morning of Eid, hugging each other and exchanging greetings, giving alms and gifts, and visiting friends, neighbours and relatives. Popular customs also include ladies decorating one's hands with henna, people dressing up in new clothes and having a good meal with family members, relatives and friends.The morning of Eid begins with men and woman taking a bath, wear the newest clothes and head for <a href="/wiki/Eid_Prayer" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid Prayer">Eid Prayer</a> then people exchange hugs and head home where a large banquet of food would be prepared. The most common foods during Eid is <a href="/wiki/Pilau_rice" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilau rice">Pilau rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicken_Korma" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicken Korma">Chicken Korma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rost" title="Rost">Rost</a>, Rezala, <a href="/wiki/Kebabs" class="mw-redirect" title="Kebabs">Kebabs</a>, Prawn Malai curry and Chili chicken, although many other dishes are also prepared. However the most extravagant arrays of dishes are dessert which consist of <a href="/wiki/Rasmalai" class="mw-redirect" title="Rasmalai">Rasmalai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rasgulla" title="Rasgulla">Rasgulla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandesh_(confectionery)" title="Sandesh (confectionery)">Sandesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firni" class="mw-redirect" title="Firni">Firni</a>, a popular Bengali dish called Paesh, <a href="/wiki/Mishti_Doi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mishti Doi">Mishti Doi</a> (Dahi) and <a href="/wiki/Faluda" class="mw-redirect" title="Faluda">Faluda</a> amongst many others. In Bangladesh family and friends visit each other's houses over the course of the 3 days and 3 or 4 houses are visited a day. During the days of Eid children receive lots of money by relatives and family friends.
For Bangladeshis Eid Al Fitr is the most awaited public holiday.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Southeast Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Idul Fitri</i> or <i>Hari Raya Aidilfitri</i> or <i>Lebaran</i> is a public holiday in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>. The customs and rituals of Eid al-Fitr are quite similar across Indonesia, Malaysia, Brunei, Singapore, the Philippines, Southern Thailand and Cambodia.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lebaran" title="Lebaran">Lebaran</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG/170px-Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG/255px-Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG/340px-Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1381" data-file-height="2268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hidangan_Lebaran.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> family celebrating <i>lebaran</i> with various culinary dishes specific to this holiday</div></div></div>
<p>Eid is known in Indonesia as <i>Hari Raya Idul Fitri</i> or more popularly as <i><a href="/wiki/Lebaran" title="Lebaran">Lebaran</a></i>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Indonesia" title="Public holidays in Indonesia">national holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-investvine_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investvine-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> People return to their home town or city (an exodus known as <i><a href="/wiki/Mudik" title="Mudik">mudik</a></i>) to celebrate with their families and to ask forgiveness from parents, in-laws, and other elders.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Festivities start the night before with chanting the <i><a href="/wiki/Takbir" title="Takbir">takbir</a></i> and lighting lamps and fireworks. On the day itself, after <a href="/wiki/Eid_prayer" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid prayer">Eid prayer</a> in the morning, <i><a href="/wiki/Zakat" title="Zakat">zakat</a></i> alms for the poor are distributed in the mosques. People will gather with family and neighbours in traditional clothing and have a special Lebaran meal. Children are given money in colourful envelopes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Later, it is common for Muslims in Indonesia to visit the graves of relatives to ritually clean the grave. Muslims also visit the living in a special ritual called <i>Halal bi-Halal</i> some time during or several days after Idul Fitri.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Malaysia.2C_Singapore.2C_Brunei_and_Thailand"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Malaysia,_Singapore,_Brunei_and_Thailand">Malaysia, Singapore,  Brunei and Thailand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eid_al-Fitr&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Malaysia, Singapore, Brunei and Thailand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_celebration.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eid_celebration.jpg/220px-Eid_celebration.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eid_celebration.jpg/330px-Eid_celebration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eid_celebration.jpg/440px-Eid_celebration.jpg 2x" data-file-width="574" data-file-height="465" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eid_celebration.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Muslims in Singapore celebrating Eid al-Fitr</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, Eid is more commonly known as <i>Hari Raya Aidilfitri</i> (<a href="/wiki/Jawi_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Jawi script">Jawi</a>: هاري راي عيدالفطري), <i>Hari Raya Idul Fitri</i>, <i>Hari Raya Puasa</i>, <i>Hari Raya Fitrah</i> or <i>Hari Lebaran</i>. <i>Hari Raya</i> means 'Celebration Day'.
</p><p>It is customary for workers in the city to return to their home town to celebrate with their families and to ask forgiveness from parents, in-laws, and other elders. This is known in Malaysia as <i><a href="/wiki/Balik_kampung" class="mw-redirect" title="Balik kampung">balik kampung</a></i> (homecoming).
</p><p>The night before Hari Raya is filled with the sounds of takbir in the mosques or musallahs. In many parts of Malaysia, especially in the rural areas, <i>pelita</i> or <i>panjut</i> or <i>lampu colok</i> (as known by <a href="/wiki/Malay-Singaporeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Malay-Singaporeans">Malay-Singaporeans</a>) (oil lamps, similar to tiki torches) are lit up and placed outside and around homes, while <a href="/wiki/Tiki_torches" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiki torches">tiki torches</a> themselves are also a popular decoration for that holiday. Special dishes like <a href="/wiki/Ketupat" title="Ketupat">ketupat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rendang" title="Rendang">rendang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemang" title="Lemang">lemang</a> (a type of <a href="/wiki/Glutinous_rice" title="Glutinous rice">glutinous rice</a> cooked in bamboo) and other Malay delicacies such as various <i><a href="/wiki/Kue" title="Kue">kuih-muih</a></i> are served during this day. It is common to greet people with "Salam Aidilfitri" or "Selamat Hari Raya" which means "Happy Eid". Muslims also greet one another with "maaf zahir dan batin", which means "Forgive my physical and emotional (wrongdoings)".
</p><p>It is customary for <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Malaysia" title="Islam in Malaysia">Muslim-Malaysians</a> to wear a traditional cultural clothing on Hari Raya. The <a href="/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group)" title="Malays (ethnic group)">Malay</a> variant (worn in Malaysia, Singapore, Brunei and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Thailand" title="Southern Thailand">Southern Thailand</a>) is known as the <a href="/wiki/Baju_Melayu" title="Baju Melayu">Baju Melayu</a>, shirt worn with a <i>sarong</i> known as <i>kain samping</i> or songket and a headwear known as <i>songkok</i>. Malaysian women's clothing is referred to as <a href="/wiki/Baju_Kurung" title="Baju Kurung">Baju Kurung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kebaya" title="Kebaya">baju kebaya</a>. It is a common practice however for the Malays in Singapore and Johor, Malaysia to refer to the <i>baju kurung</i> in reference to the type of outfit, worn by both men and women.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg/170px-Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg/255px-Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg/340px-Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Majlis_Tujuh_Likor_Pasang_Pelita.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rows of Pelita (<a href="/wiki/Oil_lamps" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil lamps">oil lamps</a>) which is used to illuminate homes and the streets during the season. Seen here in <a href="/wiki/Muar_town" class="mw-redirect" title="Muar town">Muar</a>, Johor, Malaysia</div></div></div>
